## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials mechanics / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: The variables sigma (stress), epsilon (strain), and T (temperature) point to the constitutive behavior of materials, where stress is a function of strain (mechanical loading) and temperature (thermal effects). This includes elasticity, plasticity, thermoelasticity, and viscoelasticity, often modeled with parameters representing modulus, hardening exponent, and thermal softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T + c2 (superposition of mechanical and thermal strain contributions)
- Thermoelastic with thermal expansion offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress from elastic strain after subtracting thermal strain)
- Hollomon power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (power‑law strain hardening, commonly used in metal plasticity)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield strength plus power‑law hardening)
- Ramberg–Osgood relation: epsilon = sigma/c0 + (sigma/c1)**(c2) (nonlinear stress‑strain curve, invertible to sigma form)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (exponential approach to saturation stress)
- Temperature‑dependent modulus (linear): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear thermal softening of elastic modulus)
- Temperature‑dependent modulus (exponential): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (exponential thermal softening of modulus)
- Exponential strain hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) + c2 * epsilon (initial exponential followed by linear hardening)
- Power‑law hardening with thermal softening factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * (T - c3)) (combining strain hardening and simple thermal softening)
- Arrhenius‑type thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (strain hardening modulated by thermal activation energy)
- Johnson–Cook thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * (T - c4)**c5) (coupling strain hardening and power‑law thermal softening)
- Zener–Hollomon parameter form: sigma = c0 * log( epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) ) or sigma = c0 * asinh( epsilon / c1 * exp(c2 / T) ) (constitutive models for high‑temperature deformation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening: stress decreases with increasing temperature → multiplication by a decreasing function of T, e.g., linear decay (1 - c*T), exponential decay exp(-c*T), or power‑law decay (T - Tref)**m
- Strain hardening: stress increases with strain at a decreasing rate → power‑law epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 or logarithmic growth log(epsilon + c)
- Thermoelastic effect: temperature change directly shifts the strain origin → additive term proportional to T, e.g., sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T)
- Yield plateau: stress becomes nearly constant after some strain → saturation form like c0 - c1*exp(c2*epsilon) or rational function epsilon/(c + epsilon)
- Combined thermo‑mechanical response: modulus depends on T and hardening on epsilon, often treated as product of strain and temperature functions → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T)
- High‑temperature creep: stress scales with strain raised to a power and exponential of inverse temperature → epsilon**c1 * exp(c2/T)
- Rate‑independent plasticity: stress expressed as a unique function of strain (no time derivative) → algebraic functions epsilon**c, piecewise linear, or nonlinear saturation
- Temperature‑dependent yield stress: onset of plasticity shifts with T → additive constant or multiplicative factor containing T, e.g., sigma0 * (1 - c*(T - Tref))

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT expression is:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) - c4*(T - c5) + epsilon**c6*c7*(T - c8)
```

With c2 = c5 = c8 = 316.1945..., let me denote this common value as K.

Expanding:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*T + c1*K + c3) - c4*T + c4*K + c7*epsilon**c6*T - c7*epsilon**c6*K
```

Grouping by T:
```
T * (-c0*c1*epsilon - c4 + c7*epsilon**c6) + (c0*c1*K + c0*c3)*epsilon + c4*K - c7*K*epsilon**c6
```

So the GT has terms:
- **T*epsilon**: coefficient = -c0*c1 = -31.12 * 0.05295 ≈ -1.6479
- **T**: coefficient = -c4 = -0.2255
- **T*epsilon^c6**: coefficient = c7 = 3.6293 (c6 ≈ 0.5976)
- **epsilon**: coefficient = c0*(c1*K + c3) = 31.12*(0.05295*316.19 + 1) = 31.12*(16.74 + 1) = 31.12*17.74 ≈ 552.1
- **epsilon^c6**: coefficient = -c7*K = -3.6293*316.19 ≈ -1147.3
- **constant**: c4*K = 0.2255*316.19 ≈ 71.31

So the GT basis functions are: **T*epsilon, T, T*epsilon^c6, epsilon, epsilon^c6, constant (1)**

This is crucial. The GT requires **T*epsilon^c6** as a basis function (T multiplied by a fractional power of epsilon).
